======================================================================
ANALYSIS 6: KEY - x-seq decomposition for tree root with children
======================================================================
Tree T = root[C1,C2,...,Cm]. Dyck(T) = (C1)(C2)...(Cm)
X(T) = X((C1)) ++ X((C2)) ++ ... ++ X((Cm))

Each (Ci) has xi1 = lc(Ci) as first x-step after wrapping.
x1(T) = x1((C1)) = lc(C1) + 0? Actually x1((C1)) = lc(C1)
  Wait — x1((C1)) = 1 + x1(C1) when x1(C1) >= 2
  And x1((C1)) involves pair_seq([1]+X(C1))

======================================================================
ANALYSIS 7: Compute bob(T) from children's (bobw, kw)
======================================================================
bob(T) = Σ_i bobw_i + Σ_{i<j} kw_i * size_j
where size_j = sz(Cj) + 1 (wrapped size)
  MISMATCH: ()() bob=1 computed=2
  MISMATCH: (())() bob=1 computed=5
  MISMATCH: ()(()) bob=2 computed=3
  MISMATCH: ()()() bob=3 computed=6
  MISMATCH: ((()))() bob=1 computed=5
  MISMATCH: (()())() bob=3 computed=6
  MISMATCH: (())(()) bob=2 computed=7
  MISMATCH: (())()() bob=3 computed=11

  MISMATCH: ()()()(())()() bob=18 computed=33
  MISMATCH: ()()()()((())) bob=18 computed=28
  MISMATCH: ()()()()(()()) bob=19 computed=28
  MISMATCH: ()()()()(())() bob=19 computed=34
  MISMATCH: ()()()()()(()) bob=20 computed=35
  MISMATCH: ()()()()()()() bob=21 computed=42

======================================================================
ANALYSIS 8: Tree-shape DP feasibility study
======================================================================
If we know (bobw, kw) for each possible child subtree of size k,
we can compute bob(T) for any tree via the concat formula.

The number of DISTINCT (bobw, kw) pairs per size:
  size 1: 1 pairs (from 8788 subtrees)
  size 2: 2 pairs (from 2354 subtrees)
  size 3: 3 pairs (from 1276 subtrees)
  size 4: 4 pairs (from 880 subtrees)
  size 5: 7 pairs (from 700 subtrees)
  size 6: 10 pairs (from 630 subtrees)
  size 7: 15 pairs (from 660 subtrees)
  size 8: 18 pairs (from 858 subtrees)

However, this still requires iterating over all (bobw, kw) pairs
and their multiplicities. For size N, this could be O(N * distinct_pairs).
The growth rate: size 7 has 15 pairs from 429 trees.

======================================================================

======================================================================
